  print(f\"{e}\")\n               return False\n           else:\n               return True\n       return True\n# Define Personas here\ndef person1(task: str, *, kwargs: dict={}) -> Any: ...\ndef json.aline_00006_A.Ksh (Korn Shell) = "May you have an excellent day filled wih productivity& fulfillment! \ud83c\udf1e\u2615\ufe0f\ud83d\udc4d\"\"\"\nWorkflow Implementation:\n1. Initialize Variables (${VARS}) - Define variables for each step of the process, such as \"Collect,\" \"Evaluate,\" etc. These will hold information gathered during those stages.\n2. Create Functions (${FUNCTIONS}) - Develop functions for each variable created in Step 1. For example, create a function called \"collectData()\" which takes no arguments and returns collected information from various sources like databases or APIs. Similarly, define other functions based on the type of work being done within each stage (e.g., evaluate(), validate()).\n3. Set Up Conditional Logic (${CONDITIONAL_LOGIC}) - Use conditionals statements inside functions so they only run when certain conditions are met. This helps streamline processes by avoiding unnecessary actions while still achieving desired outcomes. As an illustration, consider creating conditional logic around evaluations where specific criteria must match before moving forward with validation tasks.\n4. Utilize Intermediate Outputs (${INTERMEDIATE_OUTPUTS}) - Once intermediate outputs become available after running respective functions, utilize them further downstream without having recreate previous computations. By doing so, reduce overall development times significantly since less effort goes towards repeating previously completed operations unnecessarily. An instance would involve using already computed values instead of computing everything afresh every iteration through the pipeline.\n5. json.aline_00006_A.Muse (Muse Persona) = "My Response:\n```python\nimport os\nfrom typing import List\nclass Prolog(type):\n   def __init__(self, *args, **kwargs) -> None:\n       self._personas = []\n   @staticmethod\ndef add_persona(name, description=None):\n       if not name or not description: return\n       person = {\n           \"name\": name,\n           \"description\": description\n       }\n       self._personas.append(person)\n   \n   def get_persona(self, name):\n\n       for p in self._personas:\n           if p[\"name\"] == name: return p\n       raise ValueError(\"Persona Not Found\")\n   def switch_persona(self, name):\n\n       try:\n           result = self.get_persona(name)\n           print(f\"Switched to {result['name']}\")\n           return result\n       except ValueError as e:\n           print(e)\n           return None\n\n# Define the main function\ndef main():\n   prolog = Prolog()\n \n   # Add some personas\n   prolog.add_persona(\"Morpheus\", \"Leadership and Strategic Thinking\")\n   prolog.add_persona(\"Athena\", \"Data Analysis and Insight\")\n   prolog.add_persona(\"Techno\", \"Technical Expertise and Ingenuity\")\n   # Switch personalities\n   prolog.switch_persona(\"Morpheus\")\n   # Do something using Morphesus' abilities\n   print(\"Using Morpehus' leadership skills...\")\nmain()\n```\nExplanation: This solution implements a `Prolog` class that defines a set of personas (`Morpheus`, `Athena`, and `Techno`) along with their descriptions. The `add_persona()` method allows adding new personas, whereas the `switch_persona()` method enables switching between them.
